## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology
**Analysis**: This task models the instantaneous growth rate dP/dt of a single population as a function of time t and current population P, which is the core of continuous-time population dynamics and mathematical biology. The relationships typically involve density-dependent feedback, carrying capacity saturation, Allee effects, and time-varying environmental conditions.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth)
- Logistic differential equation (Verhulst): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (density-dependent saturation)
- Quadratic logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (carrying capacity K = 1/c1)
- Gompertz growth law: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - log(P)) (asymmetric S-curve, often in tumor or biological growth)
- von Bertalanffy growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (allometric growth with catabolic loss)
- Allee effect model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (c2 - P) (threshold at low density and carrying capacity at high density)
- Theta-logistic model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized asymmetric sigmoid, c2 controls shape)
- Time-varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / (c1 + c2 * t)) (linear change in environment capacity)
- Harvesting at constant effort: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (logistic growth with proportional removal)
- Seasonally forced growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1) + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic environmental fluctuations)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (super-exponential for c1 > 1, e.g., human population bursts)
- Logistic with Allee threshold: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P/c1 - 1) * (1 - P/c2) (combined threshold and capacity)
- Density-dependent mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - P) - c2 * P**2 (extra mortality term)
- Logistic with time-dependent rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P * (1 - P / c2) (linearly changing growth rate)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-dependent feedback: negative quadratic term -c*P**2 indicates intraspecific competition slowing growth as population rises.
- Allee threshold: factor (P - c) causes growth rate to be negative below a critical population size, capturing mate-finding difficulty or cooperation.
- Saturation at carrying capacity: term (1 - P/K) drives growth to zero when P equals capacity, producing an S-shaped trajectory.
- Per capita growth nonlinearity: dP_dt / P expressed as a decreasing function of P (linear for logistic, logarithmic for Gompertz, quadratic for Allee).
- Time-varying parameters: growth coefficients depending on t (e.g., c0 + c1*t) allow modeling environmental trends or climate change.
- Periodic forcing: additive sinusoidal terms represent seasonal breeding or resource cycles influencing growth rate.
- Harvesting/mortality removal: constant-effort removal appears as a linear term -c*P, leading to sustainable yield thresholds.
- Allometric scaling: power-law term P**c1 reflects metabolic scaling between body size and growth when P represents biomass.
- Asymmetric growth curves: models like Gompertz or theta-logistic produce skewness in the S-curve, relevant for species with rapid early growth or prolonged decline.
- Sigmoid trajectory signature: the shape of P(t) implies dP/dt as a hump-shaped function of P, peaking at intermediate population sizes for many density-dependent models.
